              ---

              In this manuscript, we present PhenoPLIER, a novel computational
              method that integrates gene-trait associations and pharmacological
              perturbation data into a unified latent space, enabling joint
              analysis. Genes function in a coordinated manner within specific
              contexts to execute their roles. A mechanistic understanding of
              expression regulation across various conditions is essential to
              decipher how these genes influence complex traits, which is vital
              for the development of new therapies. While transcriptome-wide
              association studies have been instrumental in identifying
              individual genes involved in disease-relevant mechanisms, there is
              growing evidence suggesting that gene-gene interactions
              significantly contribute to the etiology and progression of
              complex traits. PhenoPLIER's representation relies on modules of
              genes with comparable expression patterns across identical
              conditions. Our results demonstrate that diseases are strongly
              associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and
              our approach accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and
              infers mechanisms of action. Moreover, an analysis of lipid
              regulation using CRISPR screens reveals that functionally
              important players lacking individual associations are prioritized
              in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In summary,
              PhenoPLIER's incorporation of co-expressed gene groups can
              contextualize genetic associations, highlighting potential targets
              overlooked by single-gene strategies. This method provides a fresh
              perspective for interpreting genetic associations through the lens
              of gene modules, thereby facilitating the identification of novel
              therapeutic targets and drug repurposing opportunities.


              Keywords: Genetic studies, Functional genomics, Gene
              co-expression, Therapeutic targets, Drug repurposing, Clustering
              of complex traits.

              In the field of functional genomics, a comprehensive understanding
              of how genes act in concert to influence complex traits remains an
              open question. While transcriptome-wide association studies have
              shed light on individual gene-trait associations, modern models
              suggest that gene-gene interactions play a critical role in
              disease etiology and progression. Here we introduce PhenoPLIER, a
              novel computational approach that maps gene-trait associations and
              pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent
              representation for joint analysis. Our method is based on the
              creation of modules of genes with similar expression patterns
              across various conditions, allowing us to identify significant
              associations between diseases and gene modules expressed in
              relevant cell types. We demonstrate the accuracy of PhenoPLIER in
              predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring mechanisms of
              action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid
              regulation, we find that functionally important players lacking
              individual gene-trait associations are prioritized in
              trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. Our results suggest that
              incorporating groups of co-expressed genes through PhenoPLIER can
              contextualize genetic associations and reveal potential targets
              missed by single-gene strategies. This novel framework for
              interpreting genetic associations through the lens of gene modules
              has broader implications for highlighting disease etiology, drug
              mechanisms, therapeutic targets, and drug repurposing in complex
              trait clustering.

              ---

              In this manuscript, we present PhenoPLIER, a computational method
              that integrates gene-trait associations and pharmacological
              perturbation data into a unified latent space to facilitate joint
              analysis. Genes often function in coordination with one another
              within specific contexts, and understanding how they collectively
              influence complex traits necessitates a mechanistic appreciation
              of expression regulation across various conditions. This level of
              insight is vital for the development of novel therapies. While
              transcriptome-wide association studies have been instrumental in
              identifying individual genes involved in disease-relevant
              mechanisms, modern perspectives on the architecture of complex
              traits suggest that gene-gene interactions significantly
              contribute to disease etiology and progression. PhenoPLIER's
              representation relies on modules of genes with similar expression
              patterns across comparable conditions. Our findings indicate that
              diseases are strongly associated with these gene modules in
              relevant cell types, and our approach excels in predicting known
              drug-disease pairs and inferring mechanisms of action. Moreover,
              an analysis of lipid regulation using CRISPR screens reveals that
              functionally important genes, which may otherwise be overlooked
              due to a lack of individual associations, are prioritized within
              trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In summary, PhenoPLIER's
              incorporation of co-expressed gene groups enables the
              contextualization of genetic associations and highlights potential
              therapeutic targets that might be missed through single-gene
              strategies. This novel framework offers a fresh perspective on
              interpreting genetic associations via gene modules.

              ---

              In this manuscript, we present PhenoPLIER, a novel computational
              method that integrates gene-trait associations and pharmacological
              perturbation data into a unified latent space for joint analysis.
              Genes function in a coordinated manner within specific contexts to
              execute their roles. A comprehensive understanding of expression
              regulation across various conditions is essential to elucidate how
              these genes influence complex traits, which is critical for
              developing effective therapies. While transcriptome-wide
              association studies have been instrumental in identifying
              individual genes involved in disease-relevant mechanisms, there is
              growing evidence suggesting that gene-gene interactions
              significantly contribute to the etiology and progression of
              complex traits. PhenoPLIER's approach is based on aggregating
              genes with similar expression patterns across comparable
              conditions into modules. Our results demonstrate a significant
              association between diseases and these gene modules in relevant
              cell types. Moreover, PhenoPLIER accurately predicts known
              drug-disease pairs and infer mechanisms of action. Using a CRISPR
              screen to analyze lipid regulation, we discovered that
              functionally important genes lacking individual associations are
              prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In summary,
              PhenoPLIER's ability to incorporate co-expressed gene groups
              provides a new framework for interpreting genetic associations
              through the lens of gene modules, thereby highlighting potential
              targets that may have been overlooked by single-gene strategies.

              In the field of functional genomics, a comprehensive understanding
              of how genes act in concert to influence complex traits remains an

              In the field of genetic studies, there is a growing recognition
              that understanding how genes act in concert with each other in
              specific contexts is critical for uncovering the mechanisms
              underlying complex traits and developing new therapies. However, a
              gap remains in our ability to accurately associate diseases with
              relevant gene modules and predict drug-disease pairs based on gene
              expression patterns. Here, we present a novel approach,
              PhenoPLIER, which incorporates groups of co-expressed genes to
              contextualize genetic associations and reveal potential targets
              missed by single-gene strategies. We demonstrate the accuracy of
              our method in associating diseases with relevant gene modules and
              predicting known drug-disease pairs, as well as its ability to
              infer mechanisms of action. Furthermore, we show that functionally
              important players lacking individual gene associations are
              prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. Our results
              highlight the potential of PhenoPLIER to provide a novel framework
              for interpreting genetic associations through the lens of gene
              modules and shed light on disease etiology and drug mechanisms,
              ultimately contributing to the advancement of functional genomics
              and therapeutic target discovery.

              In the field of functional genomics, a comprehensive understanding
              of how genes interact to influence complex traits remains an open
              question. While it is recognized that genes often act in concert
              with each other in specific contexts to perform their functions,
              determining the precise mechanisms by which these genes contribute
              to disease susceptibility and drug response requires a mechanistic
              understanding of expression regulation across different

              our approach is accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs
              and inferring mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR

              ---

              Genes operate cooperatively within specific contexts to execute
              their functions, necessitating a mechanistic understanding of
              expression regulation across various conditions for deciphering
              their influence on complex traits. Such knowledge is critical for
              the development of novel therapies. Although transcriptome-wide
              association studies have shed light on individual genes' roles in
              disease-relevant mechanisms, the architecture of complex traits
              implies that gene-gene interactions significantly contribute to
              disease etiology and progression. In this study, we introduce
              PhenoPLIER, a computational method that integrates gene-trait
              associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a shared
              latent space for joint analysis. This approach is based on gene
              modules exhibiting similar expression patterns across identical
              conditions. Our findings reveal significant associations between
              diseases and gene modules expressed in relevant cell types.
              Moreover, PhenoPLIER accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs
              and infers mechanisms of action. Notably, a CRISPR screen analysis
              of lipid regulation reveals that functionally important genes,
              which lack individual associations, are prioritized in
              trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER.

              modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the same
              conditions, allowing us to observe significant associations
              between diseases and gene modules expressed in relevant cell
              types. Our approach accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs
              and infer mechanisms of action. Moreover, we demonstrate the
              utility of PhenoPLIER by analyzing a CRISPR screen for lipid
              regulation, revealing that functionally important players lacking
              individual gene associations are prioritized in trait-associated
              modules by our approach. By providing a more comprehensive
              understanding of gene interactions in complex traits and diseases,
              PhenoPLIER moves the broader field forward towards developing new
              therapies.

              In the field of genetic studies, there is a growing recognition of
              the importance of understanding how genes act in concert with each
              other to influence complex traits, particularly in the context of
              disease etiology and therapy development. While transcriptome-wide
              association studies have been successful in uncovering the role of
              individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms, modern models
              suggest that gene-gene interactions play a crucial role in disease
              origin and progression. However, current methods for mapping
              gene-trait associations do not take into account the complex
              interplay between genes and their regulation across different
              conditions. To address this gap, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a novel
              computational approach that maps gene-trait associations and
              pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent
              representation based on modules of genes with similar expression
              patterns across the same conditions. We demonstrate that diseases
              are significantly associated with gene modules expressed in
              relevant cell types and that our approach is accurate in
              predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring mechanisms of
              action. Furthermore, we highlight the utility of PhenoPLIER by
              using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation and finding that
              functionally important players lacking individual gene
              associations are prioritized in trait-associated modules. Our
              findings underscore the importance of considering gene-gene
              interactions in genetic studies and provide a powerful new tool
              for functional genomics, therapeutic target identification, and
              drug repurposing.

              In the field of genetic studies, there is a growing recognition of

              genomics approaches for uncovering genetic associations and
              informing drug development efforts.

              portion that highlights how this conclusion moves the broader
              field forward (e.g. "broader significance").
